            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">SnS2 has been extensive studied as an anode material for sodium storage owing to its high theor. specific capacity, whereas the unsatisfied initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) caused by the partial irreversible conversion reaction during the charge/discharge process is one of the crit. issues that hamper its practical applications.  Hence, heterostructured SnS2/Mn2SnS4/carbon nanoboxes (SMS/C NBs) have been developed by a facial wet-chem. method and utilized as the anode material of sodium ion batteries.  SMS/C NBs can deliver an initial capacity of 841.2 mAh g-1 with high ICE of 90.8%, excellent rate capability (752.3, 604.7, 570.1, 546.9, 519.7, and 488.7 mAh g-1 at the current rate of 0.1, 0.5, 1.0, 2.0, 5.0, and 10.0 A g-1, resp.), and long cycling stability (522.5 mAh g-1 at 5.0 A g-1 after 500 cycles).  The existence of SnS2/Mn2SnS4 heterojunctions can effectively stabilize the reaction products Sn and Na2S, greatly prevent the coarsening of nanosized Sn0, and enhance reversible conversion--alloying reaction, which play a key role in improving the ICE and extending the cycling performance.  Moreover, the heterostructured SMS coupled with the interacting carbon network provides efficient channels for electrons and Na+ diffusion, resulting in an excellent rate performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpbZ1R4cwpT7rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhPijZXCQAcrQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXjsVaqu7Y%253D&amp;md5=4575ad64469267af9d8a39c2100599e4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.8b03059"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Highly Porous FeS/Carbon Fibers Derived from Fe-Carrageenan Biomass: High-capacity and Durable Anodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                 <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The nanostructured metal sulfides have been reported as promising anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to their high theor. capacities but have suffered from the unsatisfactory electronic cond. and poor structural stability during a charge/discharge process, thus limiting their applications.  Herein, the one-dimensional (1D) porous FeS/carbon fibers (FeS/CFs) micro/nanostructures are fabricated through facile pyrolysis of double-helix-structured Fe-carrageenan fibers.  The FeS nanoparticles are in situ formed by interacting with sulfur-contg. group of natural material ι-carrageenan and uniformly embedded in the unique 1D porous carbon fibrous matrix, significantly enhancing the sodium-ion storage performance.  The obtained FeS/CFs with optimized sodium storage performance benefits from the appropriate carbon content (20.9 wt %).  The composite exhibits high capacity and excellent cycling stability (283 mAh g-1 at c.d. of 1 A g-1 after 400 cycles) and rate performance (247 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1).  This work provides a simple strategy to construct 1D porous FeS/CFs micro/nanostructures as high-performance anode materials for SIBs via a unique sustainable and environmentally friendly way.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoBt70HtBEZuLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhPijZXCQAcrQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXot1Ciu7k%253D&amp;md5=1e5e9d35e723d6161373f642c3a01ade</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.0c00020"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, W.                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bimetallic Sulfide Sb2S3@FeS2 Hollow Nanorods as High-Performance Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cao, Liang; Gao, Xuanwen; Zhang, Bao; Ou, Xing; Zhang, Jiafeng; Luo, Wen-Bin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3610-3620</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Constructing a heterojunction and introducing an interfacial interaction by designing ideal structures have the inherent advantages of optimizing electronic structures and macroscopic mech. properties.  An exquisite hierarchical heterogeneous structure of bimetal sulfide Sb2S3@FeS2 hollow nanorods embedded into a nitrogen-doped carbon matrix is fabricated by a concise two-step solvothermal method.  The FeS2 interlayer expands in situ grow on the interface of hollow Sb2S3 nanorods within the nitrogen-doped graphene matrix, forming a delicate heterostructure.  Such a well-designed architecture affords rapid Na+ diffusion and improves charge transfer at the heterointerfaces.  Meanwhile, the strongly synergistic coupling interaction among the interior Sb2S3, interlayer FeS2, and external nitrogen-doped carbon matrix creates a stable nanostructure, which extremely accelerates the electronic/ion transport and effectively alleviates the vol. expansion upon long cyclic performance.  As a result, the composite, as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries, exhibits a superior rate capability of 537.9 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1 and excellent cyclic stability with 85.7% capacity retention after 1000 cycles at 5 A g-1.  Based on the DFT calcn., the existing constructing heterojunction in this composite can not only optimize the electronic structure to enhance the cond. but also favor the Na2S adsorption energy to accelerate the reaction kinetics.  The outstanding electrochem. performance sheds light on the strategy by the rational design of hierarchical heterogeneous nanostructures for energy storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrwpBkuzvl5DbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhb6v7lBiMrzA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXktlOgsLc%253D&amp;md5=781fe918309ad3fe806dcdcc1b39041f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.0c04309"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Phase engineering of iron-cobalt sulfides for Zn-air and Na-ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lu, Shu; Jiang, Jun; Yang, Hai; Zhang, Ying-Jie; Pei, Dan-Ni; Chen, Jie-Jie; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable batteries are promising platforms for sustainable development of energy conversion and storage technologies.  Highly efficient multifunctional electrodes based on bimetallic sulfides for rechargeable batteries are extremely desirable but still challenging to tailor with controllable phase and structure.  Here, we report a colloidal strategy to fabricate FeCo-based bimetallic sulfides on reduced graphene oxide (rGO), which are expected to display highly efficient oxygen electrocatalysis and sodium storage performances.  Specifically, as-screened FeCo8S8 nanosheets (NSs) on rGO originating from suitable tailoring of the Co9S8 matrix with Fe at the at. level exhibited a very low p.d. (0.77 V) at 10 mA cm-2 and negligible voltage loss after 200 cycles as an air electrode for Zn-air batteries.  For Na-ion batteries, FeCo8S8 NS/rGO demonstrated a superior high-rate capability (188 mAh g-1 at 20 A g-1) with long-term cycling stability.  The bifunctional electrocatalytic property and sodium storage performance are attributed to not only the synergistic effect of Fe/Co but also the optimized catalytic activity and ion transport ability by the in situ rGO hybrid.  This work demonstrates the potential applications of FeCo-based bimetallic sulfides as efficient electrode materials for both rechargeable Zn-air and Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpy7BfT2wrSvrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhb6v7lBiMrzA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhsVCrtLrO&amp;md5=8688d9dff18619ac0173706c38c8d36b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1021/acsomega.8b01903"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kashale, A.                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Biomass-Mediated Synthesis of Cu-Doped TiO2 Nanoparticles for Improved-Performance Lithium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kashale, Anil A.; Dwivedi, Pravin K.; Sathe, Bhaskar R.; Shelke, Manjusha V.; Chang, Jia-Yaw; Ghule, Anil V.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Omega</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pure TiO2 and Cu-doped TiO2 nanoparticles are synthesized by the biomediated green approach using the Bengal gram bean ext.  The ext. contg. biomols. acts as capping agent, which helps to control the size of nanoparticles and inhibit the agglomeration of particles.  Copper is doped in TiO2 to enhance the electronic cond. of TiO2 and its electrochem. performance.  The Cu-doped TiO2 nanoparticle-based anode shows high specific capacitance, good cycling stability, and rate capability performance for its envisaged application in lithium-ion battery.  Among pure TiO2, 3% Cu-doped TiO2, and 7% Cu-doped TiO2 anode, the latter shows the highest capacity of 250 mAh g-1 (97.6% capacity retention) after 100 cycles and more than 99% of coulombic efficiency at 0.5 A g-1 c.d.  The improved electrochem. performance in the 7% Cu-doped TiO2 is attributed to the synergetic effect between copper and titania.  The results reveal that Cu-doped TiO2 nanoparticles might be contributing to the enhanced electronic cond., providing an efficient pathway for fast electron transfer.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpr82H10HdeLbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhb6v7lBiMrzA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhvFCgs7bJ&amp;md5=98c6cdad5b118d7f2369e76b752f81ff</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1021/acssuschemeng.9b02443"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ternary Anode Design for Sustainable Battery Technology: An Off-Stoichiometric Sn/SnSiOx+2@C Composite Recycled from Biomass</span>. <i>ACS Sustainable Chem.                 10.1021/acssuschemeng.9b02443</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D7%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D12563%26journal%3DACS%2BSustainable%2BChem.%2BEng.%26author%3DM.%2BBai%26author%3DX.%2BTang%26author%3DC.%2BSun%26author%3DY.%2BZhang%26author%3DW.%2BWu%26author%3DS.%2BLi%26author%3DS.%2BLiu%26author%3DW.%2BZhao%26author%3DY.%2BMa%26title%3DTernary%2BAnode%2BDesign%2Bfor%2BSustainable%2BBattery%2BTechnology%253A%2BAn%2BOff-Stoichiometric%2BSn%252FSnSiOx%252B2%2540C%2BComposite%2BRecycled%2Bfrom%2BBiomass%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facssuschemeng.9b02443&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsomega.2c06429&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facssuschemeng.9b02443&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ternary Anode Design for Sustainable Battery Technology: An Off-Stoichiometric Sn/SnSiOx+2@C Composite Recycled from Biomass</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bai, Miao; Tang, Xiaoyu; Sun, Changchun; Zhang, Yanhu; Wu, Weiwei; Li, Shaowen; Liu, Siyuan; Zhao, Wenyu; Ma, Yue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Sustainable Chemistry &amp; Engineering</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">14</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">12563-12573</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Recycling of environmentally benign, highly abundant mineral resources and low-cost biomass for electrodes is urgently needed for the sustainable integration of energy storage devices.  In the present study, a rational design is proposed of a ternary composite by integrating Sn nanoparticles, a glass-phase SnSiOx+2 matrix, and a biomass deriving N-doped carbon framework via a one-pot, scalable annealing process.  The synergistic effect of reversible Li+ storage properties originates from the complementary functionalities of each component: abundant functional groups grafted on the processed biomass anchor the metallic precursors for intimate coupling of the electroactive components, and the biomass-derived carbon framework serves as a conductive substrate for the ultrasmall Sn particles calcined from the off-stoichiometric precursor ratio while glass-phase SnSiOx+2 accommodates the vol. expansion of the Sn-Li alloy.  The Sn/SnSiOx+2@C-650 composite anode displays an overall satisfactory cycle performance: the high areal capacity of 1.68 mA h cm-2 with av. Columbic efficiency higher than 99% at 0.2 mA cm-2 and rate behavior up to 4 mA cm-2 are simultaneously realized in the half cell.  It is further established that a prototype full cell by pairing the Sn/SnSiOx+2@C-650 anode with the modified LiMn2O4 cathode, a remarkable cycling stability is maintained for 50 cycles with high gravimetric/volumetric energy densities.  This biomass-templated strategy demonstrates a precise control over the structural and compositional features of a multinary composite for next-generation batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq4PwHULoiWDbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhb6v7lBiMrzA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXht1aqsb%252FF&amp;md5=28fa6d3d279aeae44fd360df6030faa2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202000904"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Oh, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cha, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cho, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Improvements to the Overpotential of All-Solid-State Lithium-Ion Batteries during the Past Ten Years</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Improvements to the Overpotential of All-Solid-State Lithium-Ion Batteries during the Past Ten Years</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Oh, Pilgun; Lee, Hyomyung; Park, Seohyeon; Cha, Hyungyeon; Kim, Junhyeok; Cho, Jaephil</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  After the research that shows that Li10GeP2S12 (LGPS)-type sulfide solid electrolytes can reach the high ionic cond. at the room temp., sulfide solid electrolytes have been intensively developed with regard to ionic cond. and mech. properties.  As a result, an increasing vol. of research has been conducted to employ all-solid-state lithium batteries in elec. automobiles within the next five years.  To achieve this goal, it is important to review the research over the past decade, and understand the requirements for future research necessary to realize the practical applications of all-solid-state lithium batteries.  To date, research on all-solid-state lithium batteries has focused on achieving overpotential properties similar to those of conventional liq.-lithium-ion batteries by increasing the ionic cond. of the solid electrolytes.  However, the increase in the ionic cond. should be accompanied by improvements of the electronic cond. within the electrode to enable practical applications.  This essay provides a crit. overview of the recent progress and future research directions of the all-solid-state lithium batteries for practical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrgumN3HdNpt7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhb6v7lBiMrzA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXosV2ht7o%253D&amp;md5=6cccd8bd11e6ff317bcae122941345fd</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201908445"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sarkar, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Q.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Recent Progress in Advanced Organic Electrode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries: Synthesis, Mechanisms, Challenges and Perspectives</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yin, Xiuping; Sarkar, Samrat; Shi, Shanshan; Huang, Qiu-An; Zhao, Hongbin; Yan, Liuming; Zhao, Yufeng; Zhang, Jiujun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Rechargeable sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered attractive alternatives to lithium-ion batteries for next-generation sustainable and large-scale electrochem. energy storage.  Org. sodium-ion batteries (OSIBs) using environmentally benign org. materials as electrodes, which demonstrate high energy/power d. and good structural designability, have recently attracted great attention.  Nevertheless, the practical applications and popularization of OSIBs are generally restricted by the intrinsic disadvantages related to org. electrodes, such as their low cond., poor stability, and high soly. in electrolytes.  Here, the latest research progress with regard to electrode materials of OSIBs, ranging from small mols. to org. polymers, is systematically reviewed, with the main focus on the mol. structure design/modification, the electrochem. behavior, and the corresponding charge-storage mechanism.  Particularly, the challenges faced by OSIBs and the effective design strategies are comprehensively summarized from three aspects: function-oriented mol. design, micromorphol. regulation, and construction of org.-inorg. composites.  Finally, the perspectives and opportunities in the research of org. electrode materials are discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrxZtUKbEdsT7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhb6v7lBiMrzA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXht1Grtrw%253D&amp;md5=e8f2c8e2e5398d80860a7d9330a42440</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201703155"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Observation of Pseudocapacitive Effect and Fast Ion Diffusion in Bimetallic Sulfides as an Advanced Sodium-Ion Battery Anode</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis and operando sodiation mechanistic study of nitrogen-doped porous carbon coated bimetallic sulfide hollow nanocubes as advanced sodium ion battery anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lin, Xiu-Mei; Chen, Jia-Hui; Fan, Jing-Jing; Ma, Yuan; Radjenovic, Petar; Xu, Qing-Chi; Huang, Ling; Passerini, Stefano; Tian, Zhong-Qun; Li, Jian-Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1902312</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to the obvious advantages of utilizing naturally abundant and low cost sodium resources, sodium ion batteries (SIBs) show great potential for large-scale energy storage applications.  And the high theor. capacities of transition metal sulfides (TMSs) make them appealing anode materials for SIBs; however, structural collapse caused by the severe vol. change during de/sodiation processes results in poor capacity retention and rate capabilities.  Compared to the development of new materials and the improvement of their electrochem. performance, the studies on their reaction mechanisms are still rare, esp. the operando characterizations.  Herein, the synthesis, anode application, and the operando observation of the de/sodiation mechanism of a nitrogen-doped porous carbon coated nickel cobalt bimetallic sulfide hollow nanocube ((Ni0.5Co0.5)9S8@NC) composite are reported.  Such a material is synthesized via facile sulfidation of phenol formaldehyde coated Ni3[Co(CN)6]2 metal-org. framework precursors with Na2S followed by calcination.  The nanocomposite displays a remarkable specific capacity of 752 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 100 cycles and outstanding rate capability due to the synergistic effect of several appealing features.  Particularly, the pseudocapacitive effect appears to substantially contribute to the sodium storage capability.  Operando X-ray diffraction reveals the conversion reaction mechanism of (Ni0.5Co0.5)9S8@NC forming Ni, Co, Na2S, and Na2S5.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoYYlXRu5-PmLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhxBXTimsn5sA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon coated amorphous bimetallic sulfide hollow nanocubes towards advanced sodium ion battery anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Yu; Wang, Pengxiang; Yin, Yanyou; Liu, Nannan; Song, Ning; Fan, Lishuang; Zhang, Naiqing; Sun, Kening</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">150</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">378-387</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Exploring proper anode hosts with stable and ultrafast sodium storage capability is a big challenge for commercializing sodium ion batteries.  Tin-based sulfides are considered as ideal anode material for sodium ion batteries because of the high theor. capacity, while its practical application is limited to the poor cycling stability and inferior rate capability, which are induced by the huge vol. variation upon sodiation and poor cond. of those sulfides.  Herein, amorphous tin-based bimetallic sulfides hollow nanocubes encapsulated by carbon are constructed and such amorphous bimetallic sulfides show excellent rate performance (478 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1) and good cycle stability (83% capacity retention after 100 cycles at 0.1 A g-1).  Kinetic anal. reveals a pseudocapacitance-dominated sodium storage mechanism in the composite.  Such rational nanostructure design and multicomponent synergistic interaction system can inspire further development of high performance amorphous nanomaterials for batteries and energy storage and conversion devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpH1s5tSXVRy7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhxBXTimsn5sA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhtVCisbjM&amp;md5=06b20bbcf56b8f0aeb8deb04d19d9d3e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1039/c8cc04318c"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lv, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Bimetallic sulfide nanoparticles confined by dual-carbon nanostructures as anodes for lithium-/sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen-Doped graphene coated FeS2 microsphere composite as high-performance anode materials for sodium-ion batteries enhanced by the chemical and structural synergistic effect</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hou, Tianyi; Yue, Shengying; Sun, Xiaohong; Fan, Anran; Chen, Yuanyuan; Wang, Mingjing; Cai, Shu; Zheng, Chunming; Liao, Bolin; Zhao, Junmei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Applied Surface Science</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing high-performance anode materials for sodium-ion batteries with high rate capability and long-term cyclability remains challenging.  FeS2, one of the most potential candidates, is massively hindered by its intrinsically low electronic cond., poor ionic diffusivity, and severe vol. change during cycling.  Considering these issues, FeS2/nitrogen-doped graphene composite (FeS2/N-G) has been proposed, where in-situ growth of FeS2 microspheres among N-doped graphene are confined into a diam. of 1-3μm and coated with the intact and uniform N-doped graphene decoration.  Through the kinetic anal. and first-principles calcns., the heterointerface between FeS2 and N-doped graphene is found to play an essential role in improving electronic cond. and facilitating Na+ diffusion kinetics.  The uniform N-doped graphene coating also helps sustain good structural stability, which is revealed in morphol. evolution examn.  Because of the chem. and structural synergistic effect, FeS2/N-G can realize the robust and fast sodium-ion storage with delivering a reversible capacity of 251.7 mAh g-1 over 10,000 cycles at 5 A g-1.  The superior electrochem. performance and simple synthetic procedure of FeS2/N-G demonstrate the feasibility of applying FeS2/N-G as a potential anode material for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrCCEUFQoe-j7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li1C1I3c6HPvA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXitFyrtLvM&amp;md5=bd42f373bf86fd23d29a87a484f8021e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2019.12.060"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jing, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Encapsulating yolk-shell FeS2@carbon microboxes into interconnected graphene framework for ultrafast lithium/sodium storage</span>. <i>Carbon</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>159</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">366</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">377</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Encapsulating yolk-shell FeS2@carbon microboxes into interconnected graphene framework for ultrafast lithium/sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jing, Peng; Wang, Qiong; Wang, Boya; Gao, Xu; Zhang, Yun; Wu, Hao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pyrite FeS2 has been accepted as one promising anode candidate for lithium- (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to its extremely high theor. capacity of 894 mAh g-1.  However, the practical capabilities including rate performance and cycling stability of FeS2-based materials are still restricted by exaggerated vol. variation and sluggish ions kinetics.  Herein, an interesting dual-carbon decorated strategy is upgraded to address these issues.  The resultant material features a hierarchical architecture with yolk-shell FeS2@carbon microboxes as well as interconnected graphene framework (GF/FeS2@C).  By virtue of the dual-carbon protection effect and binary channel for electrons/ions transfer, the GF/FeS2@C composites exhibit superior Li and Na storage performance.  For LIBs, it shows superior rate capability of 428 mAh g-1 at 20 A g-1 and decent long-term cycle stability.  As for SIBs, it delivers a reversible capacity of 200 mAh g-1 at high c.d. of 10 A g-1 and ultra-long lifespan at 0.5 A g-1 (257 mAh g-1 after 1000 cycles) and 2 A g-1 (203 mAh g-1 after 600 cycles).                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Urchin-like FeS2 hierarchitectures wrapped with N-doped multi-wall carbon nanotubes@rGO as high-rate anode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shao, Lianyi; Hong, Junzhi; Wang, Shige; Wu, Fangdan; Yang, Fan; Shi, Xiaoyan; Sun, Zhipeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

                        cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrathin ZnIn2S4 Nanosheets Anchored on Ti3C2TX MXene for Photocatalytic H2 Evolution</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zuo, Gancheng; Wang, Yuting; Teo, Wei Liang; Xie, Aming; Guo, Yang; Dai, Yuxuan; Zhou, Weiqiang; Jana, Deblin; Xian, Qiming; Dong, Wei; Zhao, Yanli</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">59</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Photocatalysts derived from semiconductor heterojunctions that harvest solar energy and catalyze reactions still suffer from low solar-to-hydrogen conversion efficiency.  Now, MXene (Ti3C2TX) nanosheets (MNs) are used to support the in situ growth of ultrathin ZnIn2S4 nanosheets (UZNs), producing sandwich-like hierarchical heterostructures (UZNs-MNs-UZNs) for efficient photocatalytic H2 evolution.  Opportune lateral epitaxy of UZNs on the surface of MNs improves sp. surface area, pore diam., and hydrophilicity of the resulting materials, all of which could be beneficial to the photocatalytic activity.  Owing to the Schottky junction and ultrathin 2D structures of UZNs and MNs, the heterostructures could effectively suppress photoexcited electron-hole recombination and boost photoexcited charge transfer and sepn.  The heterostructure photocatalyst exhibits improved photocatalytic H2 evolution performance (6.6 times higher than pristine ZnIn2S4) and excellent stability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqjhNqkegqEsbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li1C1I3c6HPvA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Wasp nest-imitated assembly of elastic rGO/p-Ti3C2Tx MXene-cellulose nanofibers for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Wenjie; Pan, Zheng-Ze; Lv, Wei; Lv, Ruitao; Shen, Wanci; Kang, Feiyu; Yang, Quan-Hong; Weng, Yuqing; Huang, Zheng-Hong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">153</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ti3C2Tx MXene has drawn considerable attention as anode materials to store sodium ions because of the capability of accommodating the large sodium ions, enabling their intercalation without substantial structural change.  However, the limited sodium-ion storage capacity of Ti3C2Tx hinders its real application in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  To enhance its performance as anode materials in SIBs, here, the authors introduce nanopores into Ti3C2Tx sheets by sonication, and after which they assemble them with rGO and cellulose nanofibers into an elastic freestanding composite structure by mimicking the wasp nest.  The wasp nest-like structure endows the resulting composite with more accessible surfaces of electrode materials to the electrolyte.  Further, the nanopores on the Ti3C2Tx sheets and the TiO2 formed from the sonication provide more active sites for sodium storage.  As a result, the resulting composite shows a high capacity of 280 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 and remarkable cyclic life with a capacity retention of 84.8% after 1000 cycles at 1 A g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqhRD1YYDSUi7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li1C1I3c6HPvA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhsVKnsr3E&amp;md5=a4f866c4e936ecbd1c4ad3d4634070bc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2019.123453"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Haridas, A.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A flexible and free-standing FeS/sulfurized polyacrylonitrile hybrid anode material for high-rate sodium-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Haridas, Anupriya K.; Heo, Jungwon; Li, Xueying; Ahn, Hyo-Jun; Zhao, Xiaohui; Deng, Zhao; Agostini, Marco; Matic, Aleksandar; Ahn, Jou-Hyeon</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">385</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion based energy storage systems have attracted extensive attention due to the similarities in the mechanism of operation with Li-ion batteries along with the addnl. benefit of low cost and high abundance of Na resources.  Fe sulfide-based electrodes that operate via conversion mechanism showed ample potential for high energy Na-ion storage.  However, the problems related with tremendous vol. changes and the dissoln. of Na polysulfides in the electrolyte deteriorate the cycle life and limit their application in Na-ion batteries (SIBs).  Herein, a hybrid anode material, FeS/SPAN-HNF, with Fe sulfide (FeS) nanoparticles decorated in a sulfurized polyacrylonitrile (SPAN) fiber matrix is demonstrated as flexible and free-standing anode material for high-rate SIBs.  Unlike previous strategies in which FeS is encapsulated in an electrochem. inactive C matrix, this study uses SPAN, an electrochem. active material, as a dual functional matrix that can efficiently buffer vol. expansion and S dissoln. of FeS nanoparticles as well as provide significant capacity improvement.  The as-designed electrode is self-standing and flexible, without current collectors, binders or addnl. conductive agents, thus rendering enhanced practical capacity and energy d.  This electrode showed a high reversible capacity of 782.8 mA-h g-1 at 200 mA g-1 with excellent high rate capability, maintaining 327.5 mA-h g-1 after 500 cycles at 5 A g-1, emphasizing promising prospects for the development of flexible and high energy d.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tin Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries Using Natural Wood Fiber as a Mechanical Buffer and Electrolyte Reservoir</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Hongli; Jia, Zheng; Chen, Yuchen; Weadock, Nicholas; Wan, Jiayu; Vaaland, Oeyvind; Han, Xiaogang; Li, Teng; Hu, Liangbing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries offer an attractive option for low cost grid scale storage due to the abundance of Na.  Sn is touted as a high capacity anode for Na-ion batteries with a high theor. capacity of 847 mA-h/g, but it has several limitations such as large vol. expansion with cycling, slow kinetics, and unstable solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) formation.  An anode consisting of a Sn thin film deposited on a hierarchical wood fiber substrate simultaneously addresses all the challenges assocd. with Sn anodes.  The soft nature of wood fibers effectively releases the mech. stresses assocd. with the sodiation process, and the mesoporous structure functions as an electrolyte reservoir that allows for ion transport through the outer and inner surface of the fiber.  These properties are confirmed exptl. and computationally.  A stable cycling performance of 400 cycles with an initial capacity of 339 mA-h/g is demonstrated; a significant improvement over other reported Sn nanostructures.  The soft and mesoporous wood fiber substrate can be used as a new platform for low cost Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPjnqhdJ5q7rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgfzLXVNYIfcQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXosVegtr0%253D&amp;md5=b49c25ccb079701ddb3c8a22d15156ad</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1016/j.apsusc.2019.145241"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guan, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, L.-Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peng, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Coherent SnS2/NiS2 hetero-nanosheet arrays with fast charge transfer for enhanced sodium-ion storage</span>. <i>Appl.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Coherent SnS2/NiS2 hetero-nanosheet arrays with fast charge transfer for enhanced sodium-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guan, Shundong; Wang, Tianshi; Fu, Xiuli; Fan, Li-Zhen; Peng, Zhijian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Applied Surface Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">508</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered SnS2 has attracted extensive attention as promising anode material for sodium-ion storage owing to its high theor. specific capacity.  However, the practical performance is always hindered by its inferior rate capability and severe capacity fading.  Herein, a novel coherent SnS2/NiS2 hetero-nanosheet arrays on carbon cloth (SnS2/NiS2@CC) is fabricated through a facile one-step solvothermal method by controlling the synchronous growth of SnS2 and NiS2.  Benefiting from the strong coupling effect between SnS2 and NiS2, and thus the markedly elevated elec. cond. and charge transfer rate for sodiation/desodiation reaction, such composite exhibits significantly enhanced performance than its pure SnS2 counterpart as the anode for sodium-ion battery, presenting a high reversible capacity (909.2 mA h g-1 of the fifth cycle at 200 mA g-1), excellent rate capability (360 mA h g-1 at 5 A g-1) and satisfying cycling stability (588.9 and 343.2 mA h g-1 at 0.5 and 2 A g-1 after 100 cycles, resp.).  Moreover, the measured Na+ diffusion coeff. for such SnS2/NiS2@CC electrode is almost two orders of magnitude higher than that of pure SnS2@CC.  Such heterogeneous structuring for enhancing the rate performance could offer an effectively alternative way for the development of advanced electrode materials for energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqqQ4hOGNXqp7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgfzLXVNYIfcQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhvFejtL8%253D&amp;md5=3da2e59832cc5a054cfc4cc7ca971593</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2019.122590"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MXene-decorated SnS2/Sn3S4 hybrid as anode material for high-rate lithium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MXene-decorated SnS2/Sn3S4 hybrid as anode material for high-rate lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Junfeng; Han, Lu; Li, Yuquan; Li, Jinliang; Zhu, Guang; Zhang, Xiaojie; Lu, Ting; Pan, Likun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The combination of transitional metal dichalcogenides with MXene is an effective strategy to explore high-performance anode materials for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs).  In this work, SnS2/Sn3S4 hybrid decorated on Ti3C2 MXene (S-TC) was prepd. through a facile solvothermal and calcination process.  The multi-layered Ti3C2 matrix improves the electron transport capability, inhibits the aggregation and accommodates the vol. change of SnS2/Sn3S4 hybrid, while the SnS2/Sn3S4 hybrid confined in the multilayer stacks serves as a spacer to decrease the tendency of layer restacking and improves the limited capacities of Ti3C2.  Besides, the nano-sized SnS2/Sn3S4 hybrid with high sp. surface area also enhances the contact between electrolyte and electrode.  When used as anode for LIBs, S-TC demonstrates a good cycling stability (462.3 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 100 cycles) and superior rate performance (216.5 mAh g-1 at 5000 mA g-1).  The strategy in this work should provide a new insight into fabricating novel MXene-based anode material for high-rate LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrhuuAc5efRb7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgfzLXVNYIfcQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhs1OhsbzI&amp;md5=672f032faf0580463f183db2596e404f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1002/cssc.201902839"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dai, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Si@SnS2 -Reduced Graphene Oxide Composite Anodes for High-Capacity Lithium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ChemSusChem</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">5092</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">5098</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Si@SnS2-Reduced Graphene Oxide Composite Anodes for High-Capacity Lithium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dai, Jinyan; Liao, Jiang; He, Minyi; Yang, Mengmeng; Wu, Kaipeng; Yao, Weitang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemSusChem</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">One of the key challenges for the development of lithium-ion batteries is the prepn. of high-performance anode materials.  In this paper, a micro/nanostructured Si@SnS2-rGO composite is reported in which Si nanoparticles with a particle size of 30 nm are electrostatically anchored on a 3D reduced graphene oxide (rGO) network and mixed with SnS2.  The step-wise lithiation/delithiation of SnS2 provided space-constraining effects to accommodate vol. expansion and particle aggregation, thereby alleviating the vol. expansion of Si during cycling as well as enhancing the structural stability, whereas the rGO in the 3D network stabilized the composite.  The composite had a high specific capacity of 1480.1 mAh g-1 after 200 cycles at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1 and a high stability at rates of 200-3000 mA g-1.  The capacity attenuation after cycling was only 89.18 %.  A stable specific capacity (425.5 mAh g-1) was achieved after 600 cycles at a c.d. of 3000 mA g-1.  Therefore, the micro/nanostructured Si@SnS2-rGO composite is a promising anode material for use in lithium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpsRsFtdE8KGbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgfzLXVNYIfcQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXitFGqsb3N&amp;md5=87eb1968630901fb3fbe200903a91216</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2020.136730"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Size-tunable SnS2 nanoparticles assembled on graphene as anodes for high performance lithium/sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Electrochim.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Size-tunable SnS2 nanoparticles assembled on graphene as anodes for high performance lithium/sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Bing; Song, Daiyun; Ding, Yanwei; Li, Wenrong; Wang, Zhixuan; Jiang, Yong; Zhang, Jiujun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">354</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Controlling the particle sizes of electrode materials has long been recognized as an effective way to improve the cycle stability and rate property of both Li-ion battery (LIB) and Na-ion battery (SIB).  A simple 1-step hydrothermal process for the prepn. of composites with size-tunable Sn disulfide on reduced graphene oxide (SnS2/RGO) is reported.  These novel material allow to comprehensively study the effect of particle sizes on electrochem. properties for LIB and SIB anodes.  The structure, morphol., phase compns., and Li+/Na+ storage behaviors of three different SnS2/RGO composites obtained at heat-treatment times of 12, 24 and 48 h were characterized systematically.  The electrochem. reaction kinetics is demonstrated by differential charge capacity plots and apparent ion diffusion coeffs.  Surface capacitive and diffusion-controlled capacitive contributions to Li/Na ions storage are also compared.  The small-sized nanoarchitecture can promote both the charge and ions transfer and thus improve the pseudocapacitor contribution.  The reversible capacity maintains at 1211 mAh g-1 for LIB after 200 cycles and 841 mAh g-1 for SIB after 100 cycles, resp., which is superior to most of the previous reports.  This work is expected to provide a profound understanding of composite anodes with controllable dimensions and fast kinetics.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrKEEaOeBTLy7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liCK4NkVmO2cw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhsV2lsLzM&amp;md5=984f580dc17d269f9627bb862fa861d1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2020.157209"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mao, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gong, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bao, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Synthesis and electrochemical characterization of 2D SnS2/RGO as anode material in sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>J.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries (SIB) have wide applications in the field of energy storage due to their low cost.  Currently, due to its higher theor. discharge capacity, tin and tin-based compds. are expected to become SIB anode materials.  Here, 2D SnS2 nanosheets with thickness of about 20 nm loaded on reduced graphene oxide (RGO) material (SnS2/RGO) was synthesized by a hydrothermal method, which display superior properties.  When the denseness of current is 100 m A/g, the discharge capacity of the first cycle is as high as 956.1 m Ah/g, and the initial Coulombic efficiency is up to 60.0%.  From the third cycle to the 200th cycles, the capacity decline rate of each cycle is about 0.13%; after 200 cycles the discharge capacity is still 443.4 m Ah/g.  This outstanding performance is ascribed to the composite structure of SnS2/RGO, which helps to alleviate the stress of vol. change during sodium ion insertion and extn. and enhances the cond. of the SnS2 material.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrxZW9Fnc2-YLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liCK4NkVmO2cw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cobalt-doping SnS2 nanosheets towards high-performance anodes for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Liqin; Zhao, Quanqing; Wang, Zhitao; Wu, Yujun; Ma, Xilan; Zhu, Youqi; Cao, Chuanbao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered SnS2 is considered as a promising anode candidate for sodium-ion batteries yet suffers from low initial coulombic efficiency, limited specific capacity and rate capability.  Herein, we report a cobalt metal cation doping strategy to enhance the electrochem. performance of a SnS2 nanosheet array anode through a facile hydrothermal method.  Benefitting from this special structure and heteroatom-doping effect, this anode material displays a high initial coulombic efficiency of 57.4%, a superior discharge specific capacity as high as 1288 mA h g-1 at 0.2 A g-1 after 100 cycles and outstanding long-term cycling stability with a reversible capacity of 800.4 mA h g-1 even at 2 A g-1.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) and Sodium-ion capacitors (SICs) have great promise for large-scale energy storage.  However, the mismatch of electrode kinetics and charge-storage capacity between anode and cathode materials remains a challenge.  Here three-dimensional self-assembled MoS2/SnS2-reduced graphene oxide (MoS2/SnS2-RGO) anode material with fast Na-ion diffusion rate and pseudocapacitive charge storage has been successfully prepd. via a facile hydrothermal method. When tested against metal sodium in the potential window of 0.01-3.00 V, the optimized MoS2/SnS2-RGO delivers an excellent reversible capacity of 818.9 mA h g-1 at a specific current of 100 mA g-1 after 100 cycles and a superior rate capability of 555.4 mA h g-1 at 2000 mA g-1 over 500 cycles. Furthermore, a SIC composed of optimized MoS2/SnS2-RGO anode and a CC cathode reaches a high specific energy of 113.9 W h kg-1 at specific power of 561.25 W kg-1.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tin Nanodots Derived From Sn2+/Graphene Quantum Dot Complex as Pillars into Graphene Blocks for Ultrafast and Ultrastable Sodium-Ion Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Zheng; Zhang, Su; Qiu, Zhipeng; Chao, Huangfu; Wang, Lin; Wei, Tong; Fan, Zhuangjun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">38</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2003557</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Tin (Sn) is considered to be an ideal candidate for the anode of sodium ion batteries.  However, the design of Sn-based electrodes with maintained long-term stability still remains challenging due to their huge vol. expansion (≈420%) and easy pulverization during cycling.  Herein, a facile and versatile strategy for the synthesis of nitrogen-doped graphene quantum dot (GQD) edge-anchored Sn nanodots as the pillars into reduced graphene oxide blocks (NGQD/Sn-NG) for ultrafast and ultrastable sodium-ion storage is reported.  Sn nanodots (2-5 nm) anchored at the edges of "octopus-like" GQDs via covalent Sn-O-C/Sn-N-C bonds function as the pillars that ensure fast Na-ion/electron transport across the graphene blocks.  Moreover, the chem. and spatial (layered structure) confinements not only suppress Sn aggregation, but also function as phys. barriers for buffering vol. change upon sodiation/desodiation.  Consequently, the NGQD/Sn-NG with high structural stability exhibits excellent rate performance (555 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 and 198 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1) and ultra-long cycling stability (184 mAh g-1 remaining even after 2000 cycles at 5 A g-1).  The confinement-induced synthesis together with remarkable electrochem. performances should shed light on the practical application of highly attractive tin-based anodes for next generation rechargeable sodium batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGplof2PU7MVqrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liCK4NkVmO2cw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anchoring SnS2 on TiC/C Backbone to Promote Sodium Ion Storage by Phosphate Ion Doping</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shen, Yanbin; Deng, Shengjue; Liu, Ping; Zhang, Yan; Li, Yahao; Tong, Xili; Shen, Hong; Liu, Qi; Pan, Guoxiang; Zhang, Lingjie; Wang, Xiuli; Xia, Xinhui; Tu, Jiangping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Tin disulfide (SnS2) shows promising properties toward sodium ion storage with high capacity, but its cycle life and high rate capability are still undermined as a result of poor reaction kinetics and unstable structure.  In this work, phosphate ion (PO43-)-doped SnS2 (P-SnS2) nanoflake arrays on conductive TiC/C backbone are reported to form high-quality P-SnS2@TiC/C arrays via a hydrothermal-chem. vapor deposition method.  By virtue of the synergistic effect between PO43- doping and conductive network of TiC/C arrays, enhanced electronic cond. and enlarged interlayer spacing are realized in the designed P-SnS2@TiC/C arrays.  Moreover, the introduced PO43- can result in favorable intercalation/deintercalation of Na+ and accelerate electrochem. reaction kinetics.  Notably, lower bandgap and enhanced electronic cond. owing to the introduction of PO43- are demonstrated by d. function theory calcns. and UV-visible absorption spectra.  In view of these pos. factors above, the P-SnS2@TiC/C electrode delivers a high capacity of 1293.5 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 and exhibits good rate capability (476.7 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1), much better than the SnS2@TiC/C counterpart.  This work may trigger new enthusiasm on construction of advanced metal sulfide electrodes for application in rechargeable alkali ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoOlE12N6EddbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgavxYOedFasA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Urchin-like iron selenide hierarchitectures and novel pseudocapacitive sodium-ion storage anode with prominent rate and cycling properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Jian; Liu, Yongchang; Liu, Hui; Song, Yuzhu; Sun, Shengdong; Li, Qiang; Xing, Xianran; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal chalcogenides have received great attention as promising anode candidates for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  However, the undesirable cyclic life and inferior rate capability still restrict their practical applications.  The design of micro-nano hierarchitectures is considered as a possible strategy to facilitate the electrochem. reaction kinetics and strengthen the electrode structure stability upon repeated Na+ insertion/extn.  Herein, urchin-like Fe3Se4 hierarchitectures are successfully prepd. and developed as a novel anode material for SIBs.  Impressively, the as-prepd. urchin-like Fe3Se4 can present an ultrahigh rate capacity of 200.2 mAh g-1 at 30 A g-1 and a prominent capacity retention of 99.9% over 1000 cycles at 1 A g-1, meanwhile, a respectable initial coulombic efficiency of ≈100% is achieved.  Through the conjunct study of in situ X-ray diffraction, ex situ X-ray absorption near-edge structure spectroscopy, as well as cyclic voltammetry curves, it is intriguing to reveal that the phase transformation from monoclinic to amorphous structure accompanied by the pseudocapacitive Na+ storage behavior accounts for the superior electrochem. performance.  When paired with the Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode materials, the assembled full cell enables high energy d. and decent cyclic stability, demonstrating potential practical feasibility of the present urchin-like Fe3Se4 anode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGodTIt1RaLh7rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgavxYOedFasA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhtFWlsLrO&amp;md5=9b4b5e3b8fa0b71d4e6688cbad726135</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1021/acssuschemeng.8b06512"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qi, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Crab Shell-Derived Lotus Rootlike Porous Carbon for High Efficiency Isomerization of Glucose to Fructose under Mild Conditions</span>. <i>ACS Sustainable Chem.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Crab Shell-Derived Lotus Rootlike Porous Carbon for High Efficiency Isomerization of Glucose to Fructose under Mild Conditions</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shen, Feng; Fu, Junyan; Zhang, Xiao; Qi, Xinhua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Sustainable Chemistry &amp; Engineering</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A crab shell waste-derived carbon/CaO composite was synthesized by a facile one-step pyrolysis strategy.  The composite was used as a solid base catalyst for isomerization of biomass-derived glucose to fructose, which is a key intermediate in transformation of cellulosic biomass into chems. and biofuels.  Physicochem. structure of the composite was characterized by x-ray diffraction, Raman spectra, SEM, inductively coupled plasma, Brunauer-Emmett-Teller, and CO2 temp. programmed desorption.  The composite showed a lotus rootlike porous structure with a surface area of 85 m2/g and contained as high as 22.4 wt. % of CaO.  The isomerization of glucose to produce fructose with the prepd. solid base catalyst was studied, and a max. fructose yield of 29.2% was obtained from 5% glucose aq. soln. at mild conditions (80 °C and 40 min).  A 25.0% yield of fructose still could be produced even when the initial glucose concn. was as high as 20 wt. %.  Finally, the mechanism of glucose isomerization by the synthesized solid base catalyst was studied.  This work provided not only an alternative approach for utilization of crab shell waste but also a better understanding of cellulose-derived sugar transformations with solid base catalyst.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq1akmAgHb6yLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgavxYOedFasA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhsleqsLc%253D&amp;md5=3a1ebf87a87d4b3a3c25c006ad9a6d14</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2018.10.034"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Crab shell derived multi-hierarchical carbon materials as a typical recycling of waste for high performance supercapacitors</span>. <i>Carbon</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>141</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">748</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">757</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Crab shell derived multi-hierarchical carbon materials as a typical recycling of waste for high performance supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fu, Min; Chen, Wei; Zhu, Xixi; Yang, Baochan; Liu, Qingyun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">141</span>
