        </div><div class="casAbstract">The exhausting energy forces us to search for new green energy and develop energy storage and conversion technologies.  Supercapacitors with long service life and high power d. show broad application prospect.  The multi-hierarchical porous carbon materials were prepd. using the crab shell, a typical seafood waste, as the precursor, and investigated as supercapacitor electrode materials.  The crab shell derived carbon exhibited specific capacitances of 322.5 and 223.4 F g-1 at current densities of 1 and 10 A g-1 resp., indicating good capacitive performance and rate capability.  Addnl., its cyclic performance was impressive with &lt; 1% capacitance fading over 10000 cycles at 1 A g-1.  The crab shell derived carbon were further used as support to assemble SrFe12O19 for constructing a superior hybrid supercapacitor with the specific capacitance of 690.4 F g-1 at 1 A g-1, and 401.3 F g-1 even at 10 A g-1.  Furthermore, the crab shell derived carbon/SrFe12O19 composites displayed the exceptional cycling performance over 10000 cycles with 94.5% of capacitance retention, indicating distinguished capacitive performances.  Such cheap, green and high-performance electrode composites based on crab shell waste provide good prospects in energy storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpqd59JHCL6trVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgavxYOedFasA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhvFCht77M&amp;md5=f237d1b115b5e7cc282344506cdc6893</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1039/b925776d"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.-J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.-M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, W.-J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, Y.-Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, D.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, Y.-Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Highly ordered mesoporous carbon nanofiber arrays from a crab shell biological template and its application in supercapacitors and fuel cells</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Highly ordered mesoporous carbon nanofiber arrays from a crab shell biological template and its application in supercapacitors and fuel cells</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Hai-Jing; Wang, Xiao-Ming; Cui, Wang-Jun; Dou, Yu-Qian; Zhao, Dong-Yuan; Xia, Yong-Yao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2010</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">20</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">20</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4223-4230</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Mesoporous carbons with large uniform pore sizes and high surface areas are of great interest due to their potential applications in electrochem. double layer capacitors (EDLCs), hydrogen storage, sepn. and catalysis.  Here, the authors report a facile synthesis approach to highly ordered mesoporous carbon nanofiber arrays (MCNAs) by combining surfactant-templating self-assembly of org. resols with a natural crab shell hard-templating process.  The obtained materials consist of a mesoporous carbon nanofiber (70 nm in mean diam. and 11 nm in mesopore), an interspacing void of 70 nm between nanofibers, and 1 μm of pores between nanofiber arrays.  The unique structure (ordered mesopores, macroporous voids and partially graphitic framework) provides a more favorable path for electrolyte penetration and transportation, good electronic cond., as well as possess a large sp. surface area (1270 m2 g-1) and more vacancies or defects in a graphite plane, which facilitate uniform distribution of metal nanoparticles and a synergistic effect between the nanoparticles and MCNAs, and give rise to promising electrocatalytic activity as a supporting medium for Pt in direct methanol fuel cells.  The resultant materials also have excellent capacitive performance for supercapacitor application.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoz5qoG57SkE7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgavxYOedFasA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3cXlvVKjtro%253D&amp;md5=0243b6eec2d545a443d842d04ce52358</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1016/j.micromeso.2018.06.021"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, H.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">N-doping and ultramicroporosity-controlled crab shell derived carbons for enhanced CO2 and CH4 sorption</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Hee Soo; Kang, Min Seok; Lee, Seunghun; Lee, Yong-Woo; Yoo, Won Cheol</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Microporous and Mesoporous Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">272</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">92-100</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">MIMMFJ</span>;

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Highly N-doped crab shell-derived carbon nanofibers (CSCN) with enhanced CO2 and CH4 sorption capacity are discussed.  Two carbonization temps. (600 and 900°) were used to control the CSCN N-doping level; the N-content of CSCN processed at 600° was higher than that processed at 900°.  Following a judicious activation process to fine-tune ultra-microporosity (&lt;1 nm) by hot CO2 treatment, CSCN from 600° carbonization with the highest ultra-microporosity had a higher CO2 uptake capacity vs. CSCN carbonized at 900° due to its higher N-doping level, although ultra-microporosity of both samples was similar.  Similar CH4 sorption capacities were identified for both.  Very efficient, selective CO2/N2 sepn. was achieved by CSCN carbonized at 600° with max. ultra-microporosity; similar selective CH4/N2 sepn. was obsd. for both of the most activated CSCN.  As a result, relationships between the ultra-microporosity and CO2 and CH4 uptake capacity and N-doping effect were clearly elucidated.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqZGOO61Coq3rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgavxYOedFasA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtFyjtrrL&amp;md5=268a4e0d5d7f50fff88f2873fb6f09bb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1039/c8se00574e"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Crab shell-derived honeycomb-like graphitized hierarchically porous carbons for satisfactory rate performance of all-solid-state supercapacitors</span>. <i>Sustainable Energy Fuels</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>3</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1201</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1214</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c8se00574e</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D3%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D1201-1214%26journal%3DSustainable%2BEnergy%2BFuels%26author%3DW.%2BShi%26author%3DB.%2BChang%26author%3DH.%2BYin%26author%3DS.%2BZhang%26author%3DB.%2BYang%26author%3DX.%2BDong%26title%3DCrab%2Bshell-derived%2Bhoneycomb-like%2Bgraphitized%2Bhierarchically%2Bporous%2Bcarbons%2Bfor%2Bsatisfactory%2Brate%2Bperformance%2Bof%2Ball-solid-state%2Bsupercapacitors%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fc8se00574e&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsomega.2c06429&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fc8se00574e&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Crab shell-derived honeycomb-like graphitized hierarchically porous carbons for satisfactory rate performance of all-solid-state supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shi, Weiwei; Chang, Binbin; Yin, Hang; Zhang, Shouren; Yang, Baocheng; Dong, Xiaoping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Sustainable Energy &amp; Fuels</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1201-1214</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SEFUA7</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2398-4902</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Crab shells derived from discarded seafood bio-waste, are a naturally abundant and sustainable resource, but their difficult soly. limits their processing and applications, resulting in severe environmental pollution.  It is very attractive to discover approaches for reducing the threats of crab shells to the environment and even to convert crab shells into useful materials.  Herein, we attempted to convert crab shells into three-dimensional (3D) honeycomb-like graphitized hierarchically porous carbons (GHPCs) by a convenient one-step carbonization process simultaneously combining catalytic graphitization and chem. activation routes.  The removal of abundant inorgs. from crab shells resulted in a unique honeycomb-like structure, and meanwhile a high doping concn. of N element was inherited in the framework of GHPCs.  Furthermore, the simultaneous activation/graphitization treatment developed interconnected hierarchical porosity with a large accessible surface area and highly graphitized skeleton.  Benefiting from these unique structural characteristics, GHPCs exhibited a remarkable capacitive performance as supercapacitor electrodes.  The GHPC electrode delivered a high gravimetric capacitance of 367.4 F g-1 at 1 A g-1 in 6 M KOH electrolyte.  More importantly, the electrode showed satisfactory rate capability where an extremely high c.d. of 100 A g-1 for charge-discharge operation was available in both KOH and Na2SO4 electrolytes.  Furthermore, the assembled sym. flexible all-solid-state capacitor exhibited a high energy d. of 11.1 W h kg-1 and a power d. of 100.5 W kg-1, as well as a good cycling stability of 90.8% capacitance retention after 10 000 cycles in a PVA/KOH gel electrolyte.  Our approach not only relieved the environmental pollution caused by crab shells but also achieved the prodn. of a high-performance supercapacitor electrode, which was promising for industrial energy conversion and storage.  It therefore demonstrated an example of trash-to-treasure transformation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqhU9i7zj0AG7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liqVDaa3a6kog"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXktVKks7s%253D&amp;md5=0a0944ae29449064353dc24f563acbd0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2021.131765"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cai, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An in situ solid-electrolyte interphase strategy to inhibit polysulfide shuttles of FeS2-based cathode material</span>. <i>Chem. Eng. J.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>427</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">131765</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.cej.2021.131765</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D427%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D131765%26journal%3DChem.%2BEng.%2BJ.%26author%3DJ.%2BHuang%26author%3DJ.%2BZhang%26author%3DF.%2BHan%26author%3DJ.%2BCai%26author%3DY.%2BChen%26author%3DH.%2BLiu%26title%3DAn%2Bin%2Bsitu%2Bsolid-electrolyte%2Binterphase%2Bstrategy%2Bto%2Binhibit%2Bpolysulfide%2Bshuttles%2Bof%2BFeS2-based%2Bcathode%2Bmaterial%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.cej.2021.131765&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsomega.2c06429&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.cej.2021.131765&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An in situ solid-electrolyte interphase strategy to inhibit polysulfide shuttles of FeS2-based cathode material</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Jing; Zhang, Jizheng; Han, Fangchao; Cai, Jie; Chen, Yuxi; Liu, Hongbo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">427</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">131765</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1385-8947</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sol. polysulfide (PS) shuttle severely degrading cyclic performances of high energy-d. FeS2-based Li/Na-ion batteries remain unsolved problems.  It is established that an ideal solid-electrolyte interphase (SEI) layer generated on the graphite anode of com. lithium-ion batteries allows fast Li ion transport but completely isolates graphite from electrolyte.  Herein, we propose an in situ solid-electrolyte interphase (SEI) engineering strategy from a new viewpoint of isolating the FeS2 cathode from the electrolyte rather than inhibiting the dissolved PS shuttle as suggested by other strategies.  A stable SEI layer is designed to be in situ self-generated on hollow-structured FeS2/nitrogen-doped carbon (FeS2/CN) cathode by a few discharge/charge cycles in a low voltage window.  The granular SEI layer derived from decompns. of the LiTFSI-based electrolyte consists of LiF, Li2CO3 and org. components, which almost inhibits the LiPS shuttle and endows the Li-FeS2/CN battery with stable 2000 discharge/charge cycles and coulombic efficiencies within (100 ± 0.5)% except a few cycles.  Moreover, the SEI layer demonstrates its generality in drastically improving cyclic performance of Na-FeS2/CN battery.  This efficient strategy is of convenience and low cost, possessing a great potential to be scaled to industrial level.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpzs1LJIHiFtbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liqVDaa3a6kog"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhvVCmurrK&amp;md5=52a903e1713f5aebd6ea5c567bef3e8a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202107249"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Grain-boundary-rich artificial SEI layer for high-rate lithium metal anodes</span>. <i>Adv. Funct. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>32</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2107249</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adfm.202107249</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D32%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D2107249%26journal%3DAdv.%2BFunct.%2BMater.%26author%3DC.%2BChen%26author%3DQ.%2BLiang%26author%3DG.%2BWang%26author%3DD.%2BLiu%26author%3DX.%2BXiong%26title%3DGrain-boundary-rich%2Bartificial%2BSEI%2Blayer%2Bfor%2Bhigh-rate%2Blithium%2Bmetal%2Banodes%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadfm.202107249&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsomega.2c06429&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadfm.202107249&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Grain-boundary-rich artificial SEI layer for high-rate lithium metal anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Chao; Liang, Qianwen; Wang, Gang; Liu, Dongdong; Xiong, Xunhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">32</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2107249</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The sluggish lithium diffusion at the electrode/electrolyte interface is one of the main obstacles to achieve superior rate capability of Li metal anodes for rechargeable batteries.  Herein, a dense and uniform inorg. solid electrolyte interface (SEI) layer composed of ZrO2, Li2O, Li3N, and LiNxOy is constructed on the surface of Li metal via the spontaneous reaction between Li metal and zirconyl nitrate (ZrO(NO3)2) soln. in DMSO.  The abundant grain boundaries in the artificial SEI created by the multicomponent enable the rapid diffusion of Li ions at the interface.  As a result, the Li metal anode treated with zirconyl nitrate (LiZrO(NO3)2@Li) delivers a stable cycle performance of over 550 h at a high c.d. of 10 mA cm-2 and a high areal capacity of 10 mAh cm-2.  When paired with a high-loading LiCoO2 cathode (19 mg cm-2), the LiZrO(NO3)2@Li anode shows much enhanced rate performance and long-term cycle stability without Li dendrite formation.  The construction of an inorg. SEI layer with a high d. of grain boundary provides new insights for the design of high-rate and dendrite-free Li metal anodes for high-energy-d. batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrWhJ4S72z2SLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liqVDaa3a6kog"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXit1OitbnI&amp;md5=a1cd2d9079f01ff1ceb77953ecd56bc0</span></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6ef5f5d47775c-SJC">window.refViewer={'ref1':['cit1'],'ref2':['cit2'],'ref3':['cit3'],'ref4':['cit4'],'ref5':['cit5'],'ref6':['cit6'],'ref7':['cit7'],'ref8':['cit8'],'ref9':['cit9'],'ref10':['cit10'],'ref11':['cit11'],'ref12':['cit12'],'ref13':['cit13'],'ref14':['cit14'],'ref15':['cit15'],'ref16':['cit16'],'ref17':['cit17'],'ref18':['cit18'],'ref19':['cit19'],'ref20':['cit20'],'ref21':['cit21'],'ref22':['cit22'],'ref23':['cit23'],'ref24':['cit24'],'ref25':['cit25'],'ref26':['cit26'],'ref27':['cit27'],'ref28':['cit28'],'ref29':['cit29'],'ref30':['cit30'],'ref31':['cit31'],'ref32':['cit32'],'ref33':['cit33'],'ref34':['cit34'],'ref35':['cit35'],'ref36':['cit36'],'ref37':['cit37'],'ref38':['cit38'],'ref39':['cit39'],'ref40':['cit40'],'ref41':['cit41'],'ref42':['cit42'],'ref43':['cit43'],'ref44':['cit44'],'ref45':['cit45']}</script><div class="articleCitedByDropzone" data-pb-dropzone="articleCitedByDropzone"><div class="cited-by"><div class="article_content-header cited-content_header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div tabindex="0" class="article_content-title"><h2 id="citeThis">Cited By</h2><div class="article__copy"> <button class="article__copy__btn"><i aria-hidden="true" class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><div class="cited-by__content"><div class="sciteMetricsDropzone">

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The application of earth-abundant materials is strategically important for industrial manuf.  Utilizing the gelatinization and metallic complexation properties of lotus rhizome starch, a FeS2/lotus rhizome starch-derived carbon (LRSC) composite was prepd. with ultrafine FeS2 particles encapsulated in hierarchically porous carbon.  The abundant interconnected macropores and micropores in the LRSC can provide diffusion channels for ions and sufficient space for the vol. change of FeS2.  Besides, a continuous interconnected carbon matrix remarkably enhances the elec. cond. of FeS2.  Therefore, the hierarchically porous carbon-stabilized FeS2 exhibits significantly improved cycling performance compared to pristine FeS2 and FeS2 combined with glucose-pyrolyzed carbon.  The electrochem. capacity of the FeS2/LRSC composite is 923.5 mA h g-1 with a capacity retention of 90.2% after 100 cycles at 0.5 A g-1, which is much higher than that of pristine FeS2 (54.6%) and FeS2/C (32.6%).  This work offers an approach for designing cost-effective and high-performance electrodes for lithium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrUfMWKfJHWoLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhfx-XoO_wGYQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXpsFelu74%253D&amp;md5=412192275e76a92b60d0fe18b53c1644</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2019.03.096"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, Y.-l.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.-t.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, L.-s.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fei, X.-f.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, Y.-z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Y.-t.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nanocomposites based on 3D macroporous biomass carbon with SnS2 nanosheets hierarchical structure for efficient removal of hexavalent chromium</span>. <i>Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">In this study, a novel nanocomposite, carbon/SnS2 with 3D hierarchical macroporous (MCS), was successfully prepd. for rapid photocatalytic treatment of hexavalent chromium (Cr(VI)).  The 3D macroporous carbon (MC) can be obtained through a simple carbonization process of loofah.  Since the MCS has a large sp. surface area, it can provide numerous photocatalytic active sites and has excellent adsorption properties for the Cr(VI).  In addn., the excellent elec. cond. and unique hierarchical nanoarchitecture of macroporous biomass carbon could rapidly absorb the Cr(VI) from wastewater and provide electron transport tunnel for rapid charge sepn./transport to suppress hole electron recombination.  It is confirmed that such three dimensional photocatalytic material can quickly purify Cr(VI)-contg. wastewater under mild visible light irradn., with a efficiency of 63.2% Cr(VI) redn. within 120 mins.  Besides the high visible light-driven photocatalytic activity, MCS also exhibits excellent cycling stability.  In addn., the SEM images of MCS before and after photocatalytic removal of Cr(VI) indicate that the morphol. of composite was perfectly maintained and no peeling-off of SnS2 was obsd.  More importantly, this study demonstrated that MCS can be used for practical applications due to its stability and economic availability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqYZNeAa34287Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgADnDhM8JI-A"> &gt;&gt;                         rightTab-cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">FeS2 nanoparticles embedded in N/S co-doped porous carbon fibers as anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lu, Zhenxiao; Zhai, Yanjun; Wang, Nana; Zhang, Yaohui; Xue, Pan; Guo, Meiqing; Tang, Bin; Huang, Di; Wang, Wenxian; Bai, Zhongchao; Dou, Shixue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">FeS2 is a promising electrode material for sodium ion batteries (SIBs) because of its high theor. capacity, rich reserves, and eco-friendly nature.  In this study, N and S doped (N, S-co-doped) carbon fibers (CFs) encapsulated FeS2 nanoparticles (5-12 nm) and adherent FeS2 nanoflakes (denoted as FeS2@CF-NS), were synthesized by electrostatic spinning and subsequent thermal treatment.  In this structure, the FeS2 nanoparticles and the FeS2 nanoflakes shorten the Na+ diffusion distance; the N, S co-doping and defect-rich sites in the carbon fibers accelerate the Na+/e- transmission and buffer the vol. expansion during the Na-FeS2 conversion reaction.  These merits synergistically contribute to the notable sodium storage performance of FeS2@CF-NS.  As anode for Na-ion half batteries, the FeS2@CF-NS exhibits high capacity (637.1 mAh/g at 1 A/g after 400 cycles) and excellent rate capacity (431.1 mAh/g at 5 A/g).  Kinetic anal. confirms that this composite structure stimulates the pseudocapacitance Na+ storage mechanism and enables a capacitive contribution ratio as high as 92.7% with respect to the total capacity.  In combination with Na3V2(PO4)3-C cathode, the FeS2@CF-NS also achieves remarkably high specific capacity (561.1 mAh/g at 1 A/g after 500 cycles) and stable cyclability (338.6 mAh/g at 5 A/g after 5000 cycles) in full cells.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpAGqqRIU43QLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgADnDhM8JI-A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhsFKhu7fO&amp;md5=208ee1d5433c02bd79ee2e5d81460b36</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2018.06.245"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ryu, S.                 10.1016/j.jallcom.2018.06.245</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A facile synthesis of sandwich-structured SnS2@reduced graphene oxide with high performance for lithium-ion battery anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lu, Xiaojing; Liu, Dongxu; Han, Tianli; Zhu, Mingyang; Ryu, Si Ok; Huang, Jiarui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">765</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JALCEU</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A sandwich-structured SnS2@reduced graphene oxide (SnS2@rGO) nanocomposite consisting of SnS2 sheets uniformly anchored on both sides of rGO sheets is presented.  The SnS2@rGO nanocomposites, prepd. through a dipping process combining with a hydrothermal method, show good electrochem. performance, including the high reversible capability of 959.2 mAh/g at 500 mA/g over 500 cycles, and superior rate performance.  A full cell consisting of a com. LiCoO2 cathode and the SnS2@rGO anode delivers the stable capacity of ∼821.3 mAh/g (anode basis) after 200 cycles at 100 mA/g.  The sandwich-structured SnS2@rGO nanocomposite accommodates vol. changes during Li+ insertion and extn. and facilitates the rapid transport of ions and electrons. Hence, heterostructured SnS2/Mn2SnS4/carbon nanoboxes (SMS/C NBs) have been developed by a facial wet-chem. method and utilized as the anode material of sodium ion batteries.  SMS/C NBs can deliver an initial capacity of 841.2 mAh g-1 with high ICE of 90.8%, excellent rate capability (752.3, 604.7, 570.1, 546.9, 519.7, and 488.7 mAh g-1 at the current rate of 0.1, 0.5, 1.0, 2.0, 5.0, and 10.0 A g-1, resp.), and long cycling stability (522.5 mAh g-1 at 5.0 A g-1 after 500 cycles).         </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable batteries are promising platforms for sustainable development of energy conversion and storage technologies.  Highly efficient multifunctional electrodes based on bimetallic sulfides for rechargeable batteries are extremely desirable but still challenging to tailor with controllable phase and structure.  Here, we report a colloidal strategy to fabricate FeCo-based bimetallic sulfides on reduced graphene oxide (rGO), which are expected to display highly efficient oxygen electrocatalysis and sodium storage performances.  Specifically, as-screened FeCo8S8 nanosheets (NSs) on rGO originating from suitable tailoring of the Co9S8 matrix with Fe at the at. level exhibited a very low p.d. The bifunctional electrocatalytic property and sodium storage performance are attributed to not only the synergistic effect of Fe/Co but also the optimized catalytic activity and ion transport ability by the in situ rGO hybrid. Among pure TiO2, 3% Cu-doped TiO2, and 7% Cu-doped TiO2 anode, the latter shows the highest capacity of 250 mAh g-1 (97.6% capacity retention) after 100 cycles and more than 99% of coulombic efficiency at 0.5 A g-1 c.d. The results reveal that Cu-doped TiO2 nanoparticles might be contributing to the enhanced electronic cond., providing an efficient pathway for fast electron transfer.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpr82H10HdeLbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li-vj0OnmMyTw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhvFCgs7bJ&amp;md5=98c6cdad5b118d7f2369e76b752f81ff</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref11" class="rightTabRefNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit11" data-doi="10.1021/acssuschemeng.9b02443"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ternary Anode Design for Sustainable Battery Technology: An Off-Stoichiometric Sn/SnSiOx+2@C Composite Recycled from Biomass</span>. <i>ACS Sustainable Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Recycling of environmentally benign, highly abundant mineral resources and low-cost biomass for electrodes is urgently needed for the sustainable integration of energy storage devices.  In the present study, a rational design is proposed of a ternary composite by integrating Sn nanoparticles, a glass-phase SnSiOx+2 matrix, and a biomass deriving N-doped carbon framework via a one-pot, scalable annealing process.  The synergistic effect of reversible Li+ storage properties originates from the complementary functionalities of each component: abundant functional groups grafted on the processed biomass anchor the metallic precursors for intimate coupling of the electroactive components, and the biomass-derived carbon framework serves as a conductive substrate for the ultrasmall Sn particles calcined from the off-stoichiometric precursor ratio while glass-phase SnSiOx+2 accommodates the vol. expansion of the Sn-Li alloy.  The Sn/SnSiOx+2@C-650 composite anode displays an overall satisfactory cycle performance: the high areal capacity of 1.68 mA h cm-2 with av. Columbic efficiency higher than 99% at 0.2 mA cm-2 and rate behavior up to 4 mA cm-2 are simultaneously realized in the half cell.  It is further established that a prototype full cell by pairing the Sn/SnSiOx+2@C-650 anode with the modified LiMn2O4 cathode, a remarkable cycling stability is maintained for 50 cycles with high gravimetric/volumetric energy densities.  This biomass-templated strategy demonstrates a precise control over the structural and compositional features of a multinary composite for next-generation batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq4PwHULoiWDbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li-vj0OnmMyTw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXht1aqsb%252FF&amp;md5=28fa6d3d279aeae44fd360df6030faa2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref12" class="rightTabRefNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit12" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202000904"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Oh, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cha, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cho, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Improvements to the Overpotential of All-Solid-State Lithium-Ion Batteries during the Past Ten Years</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  After the research that shows that Li10GeP2S12 (LGPS)-type sulfide solid electrolytes can reach the high ionic cond. at the room temp., sulfide solid electrolytes have been intensively developed with regard to ionic cond. and mech. properties.  As a result, an increasing vol. of research has been conducted to employ all-solid-state lithium batteries in elec. automobiles within the next five years.  To achieve this goal, it is important to review the research over the past decade, and understand the requirements for future research necessary to realize the practical applications of all-solid-state lithium batteries.  To date, research on all-solid-state lithium batteries has focused on achieving overpotential properties similar to those of conventional liq.-lithium-ion batteries by increasing the ionic cond. of the solid electrolytes.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Rechargeable sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered attractive alternatives to lithium-ion batteries for next-generation sustainable and large-scale electrochem. energy storage.  Org. sodium-ion batteries (OSIBs) using environmentally benign org. materials as electrodes, which demonstrate high energy/power d. and good structural designability, have recently attracted great attention.  Nevertheless, the practical applications and popularization of OSIBs are generally restricted by the intrinsic disadvantages related to org. electrodes, such as their low cond., poor stability, and high soly. in electrolytes.  Here, the latest research progress with regard to electrode materials of OSIBs, ranging from small mols. to org. polymers, is systematically reviewed, with the main focus on the mol. structure design/modification, the electrochem. behavior, and the corresponding charge-storage mechanism.  Particularly, the challenges faced by OSIBs and the effective design strategies are comprehensively summarized from three aspects: function-oriented mol. design, micromorphol. regulation, and construction of org.-inorg. composites.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to the obvious advantages of utilizing naturally abundant and low cost sodium resources, sodium ion batteries (SIBs) show great potential for large-scale energy storage applications.  And the high theor. capacities of transition metal sulfides (TMSs) make them appealing anode materials for SIBs; however, structural collapse caused by the severe vol. change during de/sodiation processes results in poor capacity retention and rate capabilities.  Compared to the development of new materials and the improvement of their electrochem. performance, the studies on their reaction mechanisms are still rare, esp. the operando characterizations.  Herein, the synthesis, anode application, and the operando observation of the de/sodiation mechanism of a nitrogen-doped porous carbon coated nickel cobalt bimetallic sulfide hollow nanocube ((Ni0.5Co0.5)9S8@NC) composite are reported.  Such a material is synthesized via facile sulfidation of phenol formaldehyde coated Ni3[Co(CN)6]2 metal-org. framework precursors with Na2S followed by calcination.  The nanocomposite displays a remarkable specific capacity of 752 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 100 cycles and outstanding rate capability due to the synergistic effect of several appealing features.  Particularly, the pseudocapacitive effect appears to substantially contribute to the sodium storage capability. Tin-based sulfides are considered as ideal anode material for sodium ion batteries because of the high theor. capacity, while its practical application is limited to the poor cycling stability and inferior rate capability, which are induced by the huge vol. variation upon sodiation and poor cond. of those sulfides.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing high-performance anode materials for sodium-ion batteries with high rate capability and long-term cyclability remains challenging.  FeS2, one of the most potential candidates, is massively hindered by its intrinsically low electronic cond., poor ionic diffusivity, and severe vol. change during cycling.  Considering these issues, FeS2/nitrogen-doped graphene composite (FeS2/N-G) has been proposed, where in-situ growth of FeS2 microspheres among N-doped graphene are confined into a diam. of 1-3μm and coated with the intact and uniform N-doped graphene decoration.  Through the kinetic anal. and first-principles calcns., the heterointerface between FeS2 and N-doped graphene is found to play an essential role in improving electronic cond. and facilitating Na+ diffusion kinetics.  The uniform N-doped graphene coating also helps sustain good structural stability, which is revealed in morphol. evolution examn.  Because of the chem. and structural synergistic effect, FeS2/N-G can realize the robust and fast sodium-ion storage with delivering a reversible capacity of 251.7 mAh g-1 over 10,000 cycles at 5 A g-1.  The superior electrochem. performance and simple synthetic procedure of FeS2/N-G demonstrate the feasibility of applying FeS2/N-G as a potential anode material for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrCCEUFQoe-j7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgYxU5z8BqlTw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXitFyrtLvM&amp;md5=bd42f373bf86fd23d29a87a484f8021e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref20" class="rightTabRefNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit20" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2019.12.060"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jing, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Encapsulating yolk-shell FeS2@carbon microboxes into interconnected graphene framework for ultrafast lithium/sodium storage</span>. <i>Carbon</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>159</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">366</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">377</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

Herein, an interesting dual-carbon decorated strategy is upgraded to address these issues. Now, MXene (Ti3C2TX) nanosheets (MNs) are used to support the in situ growth of ultrathin ZnIn2S4 nanosheets (UZNs), producing sandwich-like hierarchical heterostructures (UZNs-MNs-UZNs) for efficient photocatalytic H2 evolution. Owing to the Schottky junction and ultrathin 2D structures of UZNs and MNs, the heterostructures could effectively suppress photoexcited electron-hole recombination and boost photoexcited charge transfer and sepn.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Ti3C2Tx MXene has drawn considerable attention as anode materials to store sodium ions because of the capability of accommodating the large sodium ions, enabling their intercalation without substantial structural change.  However, the limited sodium-ion storage capacity of Ti3C2Tx hinders its real application in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  To enhance its performance as anode materials in SIBs, here, the authors introduce nanopores into Ti3C2Tx sheets by sonication, and after which they assemble them with rGO and cellulose nanofibers into an elastic freestanding composite structure by mimicking the wasp nest.  The wasp nest-like structure endows the resulting composite with more accessible surfaces of electrode materials to the electrolyte.  Further, the nanopores on the Ti3C2Tx sheets and the TiO2 formed from the sonication provide more active sites for sodium storage.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries offer an attractive option for low cost grid scale storage due to the abundance of Na.  Sn is touted as a high capacity anode for Na-ion batteries with a high theor. capacity of 847 mA-h/g, but it has several limitations such as large vol. expansion with cycling, slow kinetics, and unstable solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) formation.  An anode consisting of a Sn thin film deposited on a hierarchical wood fiber substrate simultaneously addresses all the challenges assocd. with Sn anodes.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered SnS2 has attracted extensive attention as promising anode material for sodium-ion storage owing to its high theor. specific capacity.  However, the practical performance is always hindered by its inferior rate capability and severe capacity fading.  Herein, a novel coherent SnS2/NiS2 hetero-nanosheet arrays on carbon cloth (SnS2/NiS2@CC) is fabricated through a facile one-step solvothermal method by controlling the synchronous growth of SnS2 and NiS2.  Benefiting from the strong coupling effect between SnS2 and NiS2, and thus the markedly elevated elec. cond. and charge transfer rate for sodiation/desodiation reaction, such composite exhibits significantly enhanced performance than its pure SnS2 counterpart as the anode for sodium-ion battery, presenting a high reversible capacity (909.2 mA h g-1 of the fifth cycle at 200 mA g-1), excellent rate capability (360 mA h g-1 at 5 A g-1) and satisfying cycling stability (588.9 and 343.2 mA h g-1 at 0.5 and 2 A g-1 after 100 cycles, resp.).         </div><div class="casAbstract">The combination of transitional metal dichalcogenides with MXene is an effective strategy to explore high-performance anode materials for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs).  In this work, SnS2/Sn3S4 hybrid decorated on Ti3C2 MXene (S-TC) was prepd. through a facile solvothermal and calcination process.  The multi-layered Ti3C2 matrix improves the electron transport capability, inhibits the aggregation and accommodates the vol. change of SnS2/Sn3S4 hybrid, while the SnS2/Sn3S4 hybrid confined in the multilayer stacks serves as a spacer to decrease the tendency of layer restacking and improves the limited capacities of Ti3C2.         </div><div class="casAbstract">One of the key challenges for the development of lithium-ion batteries is the prepn. of high-performance anode materials.  In this paper, a micro/nanostructured Si@SnS2-rGO composite is reported in which Si nanoparticles with a particle size of 30 nm are electrostatically anchored on a 3D reduced graphene oxide (rGO) network and mixed with SnS2.  The step-wise lithiation/delithiation of SnS2 provided space-constraining effects to accommodate vol. expansion and particle aggregation, thereby alleviating the vol. expansion of Si during cycling as well as enhancing the structural stability, whereas the rGO in the 3D network stabilized the composite.  The composite had a high specific capacity of 1480.1 mAh g-1 after 200 cycles at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1 and a high stability at rates of 200-3000 mA g-1.  The capacity attenuation after cycling was only 89.18 %.  A stable specific capacity (425.5 mAh g-1) was achieved after 600 cycles at a c.d. of 3000 mA g-1.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Controlling the particle sizes of electrode materials has long been recognized as an effective way to improve the cycle stability and rate property of both Li-ion battery (LIB) and Na-ion battery (SIB).  A simple 1-step hydrothermal process for the prepn. of composites with size-tunable Sn disulfide on reduced graphene oxide (SnS2/RGO) is reported.  These novel material allow to comprehensively study the effect of particle sizes on electrochem. properties for LIB and SIB anodes.  The structure, morphol., phase compns., and Li+/Na+ storage behaviors of three different SnS2/RGO composites obtained at heat-treatment times of 12, 24 and 48 h were characterized systematically.  The electrochem. reaction kinetics is demonstrated by differential charge capacity plots and apparent ion diffusion coeffs.  Surface capacitive and diffusion-controlled capacitive contributions to Li/Na ions storage are also compared.  The small-sized nanoarchitecture can promote both the charge and ions transfer and thus improve the pseudocapacitor contribution.  The reversible capacity maintains at 1211 mAh g-1 for LIB after 200 cycles and 841 mAh g-1 for SIB after 100 cycles, resp., which is superior to most of the previous reports.  This work is expected to provide a profound understanding of composite anodes with controllable dimensions and fast kinetics.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrKEEaOeBTLy7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lipdyiusl7rug"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhsV2lsLzM&amp;md5=984f580dc17d269f9627bb862fa861d1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref32" class="rightTabRefNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit32" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2020.157209"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mao, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gong, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bao, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Synthesis and electrochemical characterization of 2D SnS2/RGO as anode material in sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries (SIB) have wide applications in the field of energy storage due to their low cost.  Currently, due to its higher theor. discharge capacity, tin and tin-based compds. are expected to become SIB anode materials. Herein, we report a cobalt metal cation doping strategy to enhance the electrochem. performance of a SnS2 nanosheet array anode through a facile hydrothermal method.  Benefitting from this special structure and heteroatom-doping effect, this anode material displays a high initial coulombic efficiency of 57.4%, a superior discharge specific capacity as high as 1288 mA h g-1 at 0.2 A g-1 after 100 cycles and outstanding long-term cycling stability with a reversible capacity of 800.4 mA h g-1 even at 2 A g-1.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) and Sodium-ion capacitors (SICs) have great promise for large-scale energy storage.  However, the mismatch of electrode kinetics and charge-storage capacity between anode and cathode materials remains a challenge.  Here three-dimensional self-assembled MoS2/SnS2-reduced graphene oxide (MoS2/SnS2-RGO) anode material with fast Na-ion diffusion rate and pseudocapacitive charge storage has been successfully prepd. via a facile hydrothermal method.                         rightTab-cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tin Nanodots Derived From Sn2+/Graphene Quantum Dot Complex as Pillars into Graphene Blocks for Ultrafast and Ultrastable Sodium-Ion Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Zheng; Zhang, Su; Qiu, Zhipeng; Chao, Huangfu; Wang, Lin; Wei, Tong; Fan, Zhuangjun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Tin (Sn) is considered to be an ideal candidate for the anode of sodium ion batteries.  However, the design of Sn-based electrodes with maintained long-term stability still remains challenging due to their huge vol. expansion (≈420%) and easy pulverization during cycling.  Herein, a facile and versatile strategy for the synthesis of nitrogen-doped graphene quantum dot (GQD) edge-anchored Sn nanodots as the pillars into reduced graphene oxide blocks (NGQD/Sn-NG) for ultrafast and ultrastable sodium-ion storage is reported.  Sn nanodots (2-5 nm) anchored at the edges of "octopus-like" GQDs via covalent Sn-O-C/Sn-N-C bonds function as the pillars that ensure fast Na-ion/electron transport across the graphene blocks.  Moreover, the chem. and spatial (layered structure) confinements not only suppress Sn aggregation, but also function as phys. barriers for buffering vol. change upon sodiation/desodiation.  Consequently, the NGQD/Sn-NG with high structural stability exhibits excellent rate performance (555 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 and 198 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1) and ultra-long cycling stability (184 mAh g-1 remaining even after 2000 cycles at 5 A g-1).  The confinement-induced synthesis together with remarkable electrochem. performances should shed light on the practical application of highly attractive tin-based anodes for next generation rechargeable sodium batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGplof2PU7MVqrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liMiNIBDYPPMA"> &gt;&gt;                         rightTab-cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anchoring SnS2 on TiC/C Backbone to Promote Sodium Ion Storage by Phosphate Ion Doping</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shen, Yanbin; Deng, Shengjue; Liu, Ping; Zhang, Yan; Li, Yahao; Tong, Xili; Shen, Hong; Liu, Qi; Pan, Guoxiang; Zhang, Lingjie; Wang, Xiuli; Xia, Xinhui; Tu, Jiangping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Tin disulfide (SnS2) shows promising properties toward sodium ion storage with high capacity, but its cycle life and high rate capability are still undermined as a result of poor reaction kinetics and unstable structure.  In this work, phosphate ion (PO43-)-doped SnS2 (P-SnS2) nanoflake arrays on conductive TiC/C backbone are reported to form high-quality P-SnS2@TiC/C arrays via a hydrothermal-chem. vapor deposition method.  By virtue of the synergistic effect between PO43- doping and conductive network of TiC/C arrays, enhanced electronic cond. and enlarged interlayer spacing are realized in the designed P-SnS2@TiC/C arrays.  Moreover, the introduced PO43- can result in favorable intercalation/deintercalation of Na+ and accelerate electrochem. reaction kinetics.  Notably, lower bandgap and enhanced electronic cond. owing to the introduction of PO43- are demonstrated by d. function theory calcns. and UV-visible absorption spectra.  In view of these pos. factors above, the P-SnS2@TiC/C electrode delivers a high capacity of 1293.5 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 and exhibits good rate capability (476.7 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1), much better than the SnS2@TiC/C counterpart.  This work may trigger new enthusiasm on construction of advanced metal sulfide electrodes for application in rechargeable alkali ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoOlE12N6EddbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liMiNIBDYPPMA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhslOqurrN&amp;md5=7d80004da1642e3f106add1c1369f268</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref38" class="rightTabRefNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit38" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202000504"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xing, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Urchin-Like Fe3 Se4 Hierarchitectures: A Novel Pseudocapacitive Sodium-Ion Storage Anode with Prominent Rate and Cycling Properties</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>16</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2000504</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        rightTab-cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Urchin-like iron selenide hierarchitectures and novel pseudocapacitive sodium-ion storage anode with prominent rate and cycling properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Jian; Liu, Yongchang; Liu, Hui; Song, Yuzhu; Sun, Shengdong; Li, Qiang; Xing, Xianran; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal chalcogenides have received great attention as promising anode candidates for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  However, the undesirable cyclic life and inferior rate capability still restrict their practical applications.  The design of micro-nano hierarchitectures is considered as a possible strategy to facilitate the electrochem. reaction kinetics and strengthen the electrode structure stability upon repeated Na+ insertion/extn.  Herein, urchin-like Fe3Se4 hierarchitectures are successfully prepd. and developed as a novel anode material for SIBs.  Impressively, the as-prepd. urchin-like Fe3Se4 can present an ultrahigh rate capacity of 200.2 mAh g-1 at 30 A g-1 and a prominent capacity retention of 99.9% over 1000 cycles at 1 A g-1, meanwhile, a respectable initial coulombic efficiency of ≈100% is achieved.  Through the conjunct study of in situ X-ray diffraction, ex situ X-ray absorption near-edge structure spectroscopy, as well as cyclic voltammetry curves, it is intriguing to reveal that the phase transformation from monoclinic to amorphous structure accompanied by the pseudocapacitive Na+ storage behavior accounts for the superior electrochem. performance.  When paired with the Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode materials, the assembled full cell enables high energy d. and decent cyclic stability, demonstrating potential practical feasibility of the present urchin-like Fe3Se4 anode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGodTIt1RaLh7rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liMiNIBDYPPMA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhtFWlsLrO&amp;md5=9b4b5e3b8fa0b71d4e6688cbad726135</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref39" class="rightTabRefNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit39" data-doi="10.1021/acssuschemeng.8b06512"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qi, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Crab Shell-Derived Lotus Rootlike Porous Carbon for High Efficiency Isomerization of Glucose to Fructose under Mild Conditions</span>. <i>ACS Sustainable Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A crab shell waste-derived carbon/CaO composite was synthesized by a facile one-step pyrolysis strategy.  The composite was used as a solid base catalyst for isomerization of biomass-derived glucose to fructose, which is a key intermediate in transformation of cellulosic biomass into chems. and biofuels.  Physicochem. structure of the composite was characterized by x-ray diffraction, Raman spectra, SEM, inductively coupled plasma, Brunauer-Emmett-Teller, and CO2 temp. programmed desorption.  The composite showed a lotus rootlike porous structure with a surface area of 85 m2/g and contained as high as 22.4 wt. % of CaO.  The isomerization of glucose to produce fructose with the prepd. solid base catalyst was studied, and a max. fructose yield of 29.2% was obtained from 5% glucose aq. soln. at mild conditions (80 °C and 40 min).  A 25.0% yield of fructose still could be produced even when the initial glucose concn. was as high as 20 wt. %.  Finally, the mechanism of glucose isomerization by the synthesized solid base catalyst was studied.  This work provided not only an alternative approach for utilization of crab shell waste but also a better understanding of cellulose-derived sugar transformations with solid base catalyst.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq1akmAgHb6yLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liMiNIBDYPPMA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhsleqsLc%253D&amp;md5=3a1ebf87a87d4b3a3c25c006ad9a6d14</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref40" class="rightTabRefNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit40" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2018.10.034"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Crab shell derived multi-hierarchical carbon materials as a typical recycling of waste for high performance supercapacitors</span>. <i>Carbon</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>141</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">748</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">757</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The exhausting energy forces us to search for new green energy and develop energy storage and conversion technologies.  Supercapacitors with long service life and high power d. show broad application prospect.  The multi-hierarchical porous carbon materials were prepd. using the crab shell, a typical seafood waste, as the precursor, and investigated as supercapacitor electrode materials.  The crab shell derived carbon exhibited specific capacitances of 322.5 and 223.4 F g-1 at current densities of 1 and 10 A g-1 resp., indicating good capacitive performance and rate capability.  Addnl., its cyclic performance was impressive with &lt; 1% capacitance fading over 10000 cycles at 1 A g-1.  The crab shell derived carbon were further used as support to assemble SrFe12O19 for constructing a superior hybrid supercapacitor with the specific capacitance of 690.4 F g-1 at 1 A g-1, and 401.3 F g-1 even at 10 A g-1.  Furthermore, the crab shell derived carbon/SrFe12O19 composites displayed the exceptional cycling performance over 10000 cycles with 94.5% of capacitance retention, indicating distinguished capacitive performances.  Such cheap, green and high-performance electrode composites based on crab shell waste provide good prospects in energy storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpqd59JHCL6trVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liMiNIBDYPPMA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhvFCht77M&amp;md5=f237d1b115b5e7cc282344506cdc6893</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref41" class="rightTabRefNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit41" data-doi="10.1039/b925776d"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.-J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.-M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, W.-J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, Y.-Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, D.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, Y.-Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Highly ordered mesoporous carbon nanofiber arrays from a crab shell biological template and its application in supercapacitors and fuel cells</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Mesoporous carbons with large uniform pore sizes and high surface areas are of great interest due to their potential applications in electrochem. double layer capacitors (EDLCs), hydrogen storage, sepn. and catalysis.  Here, the authors report a facile synthesis approach to highly ordered mesoporous carbon nanofiber arrays (MCNAs) by combining surfactant-templating self-assembly of org. resols with a natural crab shell hard-templating process.  The obtained materials consist of a mesoporous carbon nanofiber (70 nm in mean diam. and 11 nm in mesopore), an interspacing void of 70 nm between nanofibers, and 1 μm of pores between nanofiber arrays.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Highly N-doped crab shell-derived carbon nanofibers (CSCN) with enhanced CO2 and CH4 sorption capacity are discussed.  Two carbonization temps. (600 and 900°) were used to control the CSCN N-doping level; the N-content of CSCN processed at 600° was higher than that processed at 900°.  Following a judicious activation process to fine-tune ultra-microporosity (&lt;1 nm) by hot CO2 treatment, CSCN from 600° carbonization with the highest ultra-microporosity had a higher CO2 uptake capacity vs. CSCN carbonized at 900° due to its higher N-doping level, although ultra-microporosity of both samples was similar.
